Asset forfeiture, as established under various state and federal statutes, is intended to disrupt 
criminal activities through the seizure and forfeiture of the instruments or proceeds of crime. 
California’s asset forfeiture statute, section 1 1 495 of the Health and Safety Code, requires the 
California Department of Justice (DOJ) to publish an annual report that provides the following information for the state and each city and county: 
•
 The number of forfeiture actions initiated during the report year. 
• The number of cases and the administrative number or court docket number of each 
case for which forfeiture was ordered or declared during the report year. 
• The number of suspects, the number of charges, and the disposition of cases. 
• The number of alleged criminal offenses that were under federal or state law. • The disposition of cases, including no charge, dropped charges, acquittal, plea 
agreement, jury conviction, or other. 
• The value of the assets forfeited during the report year. • The dates of the disbursements, the recipients of the funds and the amounts received. 
The 25th annual report covers the 2019 calendar year. DOJ received federal seizure and 
forfeiture information from 33 out of approximately 400 local law enforcement agencies, and state seizure and forfeiture information from 48 out of 58 district attorneys’ offces. 
1  Health and Safety Code Section 11495 
1 1 495. (a) The funds received by the law enforcement agencies under section 1 1 489 
shall be deposited into an account maintained by the Controller, county auditor, or 
city treasurer. These funds shall be distributed to the law enforcement agencies at their request. The Controller, auditor, or treasurer shall maintain a record of these disbursements which records shall be open to public inspection, subject to the privileges contained in sections 1040, 1041, and 1042 of the Evidence Code. 
(b) Upon request of the governing body of the jurisdiction in which the distributions are 
made, the Controller, auditor, or treasurer shall conduct an audit of these funds and their use. In the case of the state, the governing body shall be the Legislature. 
(c) Each year, the Attorney General shall publish a report which sets forth the following 
information for the state, each county, each city, and each city and county:  
(1) The number of forfeiture actions initiated and administered by state or local 
agencies under California law, the number of cases adopted by the federal government, and the number of cases initiated by a joint federal-state action that were prosecuted under federal law. 
(2) The number of cases and the administrative number or court docket number of 
each case for which forfeiture was ordered or declared. 
(3) The number of suspects charged with a controlled substance violation. 
(4) The number of alleged criminal offenses that were under federal or state law. (5) The disposition of cases, including no charge, dropped charges, acquittal, plea 
agreement, jury conviction, or other. 
(6) The value of the assets forfeited. (7) The recipients of the forfeited assets, the amounts received, and the date of 
the disbursement. 
(d) The Attorney General shall develop administrative guidelines for the collection and 
publication of the information required in subdivision (c). 
(e) The Attorney General’s report shall cover the calendar year and shall be made no 
later than July 1 of each year beginning with the year after the enactment of this law. 
2 3 
 
 
  
    
      
        
    
        
        
     
       
   
Statistics were solicited from California’s district attorneys’ offces and law enforcement  
agencies. Although DOJ is required to prepare this report, local agencies are not statutorily  
mandated to provide their data to DOJ for inclusion. The 2019 report refects the responses that  
were received from 48 district attorneys and 33 law enforcement agencies. In California, there  
are 58 district attorneys and approximately 400 law enforcement agencies. Based on this  
sample of counties and localities, the following highlights the fndings in this report: 
• A total of 2,5
79 state forfeiture proceedings were initiated in 2019 (Table 1). 
• A total of 1, 17 1 federal forfeiture sharing requests were submitted in 2019 (Table 4). 
• A total of 2, 1 89 state forfeiture cases were completed during 2019, which included 
cases initiated in 2019 and prior years. The total value of the disbursed assets is $30, 1 1 1, 164 (Table 2). 
• A total of 737 joint federal asset forfeiture cases in which state or local law enforcement participated were completed and disbursed during 2019. The total value of the federal equitable sharing funds received is $1 4,824, 193 (Table 5). 
• Alpine, Inyo and Sierra counties reported no state forfeiture cases initiated or completed in 2019 (Table 3). 
• The following ten counties did not participate in providing data for this report: Calaveras, Del Norte, Mariposa, Merced, Mono, San Benito, San Luis Obispo, Santa Clara, Sutter and Yuba. 
• A total of 33 law enforcement agencies participated in this report, seven of which reported no federal equitable sharing funds received (Table 6).   
 
  
  
  
To comply with the requirements of Heath and Safety Code section 1 1 495, DOJ reached 
out to all California district attorneys, the offcials conducting state forfeiture proceedings, to request that they provide DOJ with the required information for each state forfeiture action conducted during the reporting period. Although DOJ is required to prepare this report, local agencies are not statutorily mandated to provide their data to DOJ for inclusion. 
Information regarding federal equitable sharing sought and received by California law  
enforcement agencies through joint investigations can only be obtained directly from the  
participating agencies. This is the second report to include federal forfeiture data and the 
second time agencies other than district attorneys’ offces have been called upon to participate.  
This report provides the information required by Health and Safety Code section 1 1 495 on all forfeitures initiated during calendar year 2019. For state forfeitures completed and federal distributions received during calendar year 2019, detailed information is provided. 
Pursuant to Health and Safety Code section 1 1 489, State asset forfeiture proceeds are 
distributed as follows: 
•
One percent to a private, nonproft organization composed of local prosecutors for the exclusive purpose of providing a statewide program of education and training for prosecutors and law enforcement in the ethics and proper use of State asset forfeiture laws. 
•Ten percent to the prosecutorial agency that processes the forfeiture action. 
•Twenty-four percent to the State General Fund. •Sixty-fve percent to the state and/or local law enforcement agencies that participated 
in the seizure of the assets, distributed in a manner that refects the proportionate 
contribution of each agency. Fifteen percent
1 of the funds distributed to law 
enforcement must be deposited in a special fund which is maintained by a council made up of local government entities. This fund shall be used for the sole purpose of funding programs designed to combat drug abuse and divert gang activity. 
1 Some counties have reported the deposit of 1 5 percent of their share to a special fund while others have not, nor are they required to.

Federal asset forfeiture proceeds received by a state or local law enforcement agency may be 
utilized for allowable law enforcement purposes as defned in the Federal Guide to Equitable Sharing. Health and Safety Code section 1 1 47 1.2 prohibits state and local law enforcement agencies from seeking federal adoption of asset seizures. It also prohibits acceptance of federal equitable sharing distributions when the asset seized is real property or less than $40,000 in cash or other negotiable instruments, unless the underlying criminal case has resulted in a conviction. When such seizures are ordered forfeited, the participating California agency must decline or return the distribution. In those cases, the entire forfeited amount is retained by the federal agency.

 constitutes the initiation of a forfeiture action. 
•  Initiated cases can be forfeited in the 2019 reporting year or remain pending after 2019. 
•  Table 1 provides information on asset forfeiture actions initiated pursuant to California   
 law during 2019. 
•  Table 4 provides information on forfeiture sharing requests initiated as a part of a joint   
 federal asset forfeiture investigation during 2019.

•  For purposes of this report, an asset forfeiture case is considered completed when   
 forfeiture has been ordered or declared and all assets have been distributed2  by the  
 district attorney’s offce or federal sharing funds have been received3 . 
•  Table 2 provides summary information on asset forfeiture actions completed pursuant to  
 California law during 20 1 9. This includes disbursement information on cases initiated in  
 20 1 9 and prior years. 
•  Table 3 is the most extensive section within this report and provides detailed information  
 on each asset forfeiture case that was completed pursuant to state law during 20 1 9. 
•  Table 5 provides summary information on federal asset forfeitures received by state and  
 local law enforcement agencies as part of a joint asset forfeiture case in 20 1 9, including  
 cases initiated in 20 1 9 and prior years. 
•  Table 6 provides detailed information on federal asset forfeiture cases for which   
 equitable sharing funds were disbursed to California law enforcement agencies  
 during 20 1 9. 
•  Cases for which only a partial distribution was made during 20 1 9 are not listed in   
 Tables 3 or 6, as they are considered still pending. They will be reported once they are  
 fully distributed.  
2 When all seized items have been returned to the defendant following adjudication of a 
previously initiated case, it is no longer considered to be an asset forfeiture case. 
3 Federal sharing funds that a state or local law enforcement agency has returned to the federal sharing agency are not considered funds received and are not included in this report.
